  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_88746fcb-5338-4e94-9ccf-55c18a874f0d'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/7324068-mj">MJ</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Gamache reads people very well and he could tell through her behavior that she was not a team player. He only wants team players working with him and <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Gamache reads people very well and he could tell through her behavior that she was not a team player. He only wants team players working with him and people willing to admit they are wrong. Based on her not being able to see that SHE may be the problem (when looking at her reflection in the mirror and then the window), it was obvious that she is self-centered and not willing to she herself as ever being wrong.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_312243484" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/312243484" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/312243484?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of pastoral mysteries</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to carol.  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus">Richard Derus</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=friend-recommended">friend-recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=awards">awards</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer312243484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18174216300806669108"><br/>Middling books are the hardest to review, dontchathink?<br/><br/>Maybe it's the recent time change (is there any point to Daylight Savings Time anymore?), maybe it's the fact that I feel like I'm swimming uphill in my nursing clinical trying to get hours in, but <i>Still Life</i> kept putting me to sleep. A blurb (or a review, I forget which) compares her to Agatha Christie, which I suppose could be true, only it's a version of Christie that was being paid by the word and operates only inside people's heads, whi</span>
  <span id="freeText18174216300806669108" style="display:none"><br />Middling books are the hardest to review, dontchathink?<br /><br />Maybe it's the recent time change (is there any point to Daylight Savings Time anymore?), maybe it's the fact that I feel like I'm swimming uphill in my nursing clinical trying to get hours in, but <i>Still Life</i> kept putting me to sleep. A blurb (or a review, I forget which) compares her to Agatha Christie, which I suppose could be true, only it's a version of Christie that was being paid by the word and operates only inside people's heads, which really isn't Christie at all. <br /><br />Consider Christie's brief character description from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16315.Crooked_House" title="Crooked House by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Crooked House</a> about Uncle Roger, an emotional gentle giant: <b>“He collided with a screen, said ‘I beg your pardon’ to it in a flustered manner, and went out of the room. It was rather like the exit of a bumble bee and left a noticeable silence behind it.”</b> <br /><br />In <i>Still Life,</i> we get characters musing: <b>"The studio was growing cold and Clara wondered whether Peter, sitting across the hall in his own studio was also cold. He would almost certainly, she thought with a twang of envy, be working too hard to notice. He never seemed to suffer from the uncertainty that could freeze her, leave her stuck and frozen in place. He just kept putting one foot in front of the other, producing his excruciatingly detailed works that sold for thousands in Montreal. It took him months to do each piece, he was so painfully precise and methodical. She'd given him a roller for his birthday one year and told him to paint faster. He didn't seem to appreciate the joke. Perhaps because it wasn't entirely a joke." </b> <br /><br />Goodness, no wonder I kept falling asleep. There is a great deal of telling and hardly any showing. Dialogue is employed when it comes time to discover items of significance or sum up progress. Inspector Gamache, who I liked strictly because his name bears a resemblance to 'ganache,' holds an informal inquest and meets with all the villagers togther, reviewing the circumstances of the death. Later, he convenes with his team, reviewing clues brainstorming solutions. For those who fell asleep earlier, it's a nice chance to catch up.<br /><br />The plot is fine; nothing unusual. It is possibly even a bit predictable--as I've mentioned before, if I can figure out what the mystery is, it must be relatively simple. I did like a development near the end that further fleshed out a character. However, many of the characters were one note: the urbane gay couple that ran a bistro and whose main conversation seemed to be joking about being gay; the petulant, money-grabbing niece; the caustic village witch--I mean 'poet.' There was also a junior detective whose characterization was particularly strange. I thought perhaps she was involved to block a crucial plot point, but I think I was wrong. Overall, I'd have to say the Christie comparison wears thin. It's not that Christie wouldn't have had weak characters, just that in her best works they would have felt a little less farcical.<br /><br />Overall though, it's a nice little study of the small village of Three Pines in Quebec, and of the talented Inspector and his team. A bit too pastoral for my own tastes, it's a bit more like a painting of a haystack at sunset instead of a group of women dancing. To combat the sleepies I started reading from the end, hoping to find a strong finish that would invigorate me (it's kind of like hopscotch, a chapter or two, then flip back further). And while it did, I have no real interest in re-reading.<br /><br />I'll give the next couple a try, because my mom wants to give them a go and because my friends seem to enjoy the series. Of course, your own mileage may vary. Note that it won a first book award or two.<br /><br />Two, two-and-a-half stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18174216300806669108" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_812777884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/812777884" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26175098-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453924875p2/26175098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/812777884?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/26175098-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=1st-of-series">1st-of-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=canadian">canadian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=own-on-shelf">own-on-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer812777884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5987585576401950953">4.5 stars<br/><br/>With the encouragement of several of my Goodreads friends, I finally decided to pick up Still Life, a novel I bought 3 years ago. I don’t know why I waited so long to dust it off, especially since it has won multiple awards, but I can tell you it won’t take 3 years for me to read book 2 of what I believe will be a highly enjoyable series.<br/><br/>Some readers called this a cozy. I respectfully disagree; I think this story is more in the category of literary mystery. There is so much depth. The s</span>
  <span id="freeText5987585576401950953" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />With the encouragement of several of my Goodreads friends, I finally decided to pick up Still Life, a novel I bought 3 years ago. I don’t know why I waited so long to dust it off, especially since it has won multiple awards, but I can tell you it won’t take 3 years for me to read book 2 of what I believe will be a highly enjoyable series.<br /><br />Some readers called this a cozy. I respectfully disagree; I think this story is more in the category of literary mystery. There is so much depth. The setting is a small village nestled somewhere in Quebec, not terribly far from Montreal. Three Pines is inhabited by a somewhat quirky group of people who have layers upon layers of interpersonal relationships. Having no local detective, the town calls in Chief Inspector Armand Gamache from Montreal when a woman is killed—was it an accident or murder? I have fallen in love with this guy. He is not your usual law enforcement protagonist with demons seeping out of his pores. In fact, he seems very well adjusted and even has a wonderful relationship with his wife (we just get a peek at the latter and I am hoping to see more of Armand’s and his spouse’s marital relationship in future books). Armand is highly intelligent, extremely perceptive, kind and gentle, yet firm and no nonsense when called for. His integrity is impeccable. I also became quite fond of his right hand man, Jean Guy Beauvoir. Overall, characterization is excellent, but not quite strong enough to pull me hook line and sinker into the lives of the villagers, perhaps only because of the sheer number of players. I do feel that Ms. Penny’s writing is such that this will come with later installments as we get to know the townfolk better. <br /><br />The plot is engaging and had me changing my mind right and left regarding whom the baddie was. I never did get it right. I did have to suspend belief just a bit regarding the intricacies of the crime, but this didn’t lessen my enjoyment of the journey.<br /><br />I enjoyed this novel more than my usual 4-star reads, but I have a feeling Ms. Perry is going to get better and better. Thus, the round down from 4.5 to 4 stars.<br /><br />Will I continue with the series? Absolutely. Do I recommend Still Life? I sure do—to all readers of crime fiction interested in something a little different and with emphasis on characterization. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5987585576401950953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_100753738" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100753738" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100753738?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780312352554" href="/book/show/912984.Still_Life">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      Harper Bell
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=mysteries-thrillers-horror">mysteries-thrillers-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100753738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4029160518530218752">I am a little sad that I can't give <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/338691.Still_Life__Armand_Gamache___1_' title='Still Life (Armand Gamache, #1) by Louise Penny' rel='nofollow noopener'>Still Life</a> more than 2 stars. It was recommended to me and it's not a pleasant task to trash someone's suggestion, but what can I do, this book was just a barely OK read for me.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/338691.Still_Life__Armand_Gamache___1_' title='Still Life (Armand Gamache, #1) by Louise Penny' rel='nofollow noopener'>Still Life</a> is a traditional ("cozy") mystery set in a Canadian village Three Pines. One Sunday morning a body of 76-year old Jane Neal - a long-time resident of the village - is found. At first, it appears that Jane was killed in a hunting accident, but later we find out that quite a fe</span>
  <span id="freeText4029160518530218752" style="display:none">I am a little sad that I can't give <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/338691.Still_Life__Armand_Gamache___1_" title="Still Life (Armand Gamache, #1) by Louise Penny" rel="nofollow noopener">Still Life</a> more than 2 stars. It was recommended to me and it's not a pleasant task to trash someone's suggestion, but what can I do, this book was just a barely OK read for me.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/338691.Still_Life__Armand_Gamache___1_" title="Still Life (Armand Gamache, #1) by Louise Penny" rel="nofollow noopener">Still Life</a> is a traditional ("cozy") mystery set in a Canadian village Three Pines. One Sunday morning a body of 76-year old Jane Neal - a long-time resident of the village - is found. At first, it appears that Jane was killed in a hunting accident, but later we find out that quite a few seemingly ordinary and upstanding villagers have some secrets to hide and maybe reasons to murder the old lady.<br /><br />On a positive side, I enjoyed learning a little about Quebec. I personally never knew that there was a tension between Quebec and the rest of Canada and also a lot of friction between francophones and anglophones. Archery/hunting details were interesting as well. And, the most exciting thing, I could practice my newly acquired basic French skills - I even knew what boulangerie was!<br /><br />As for the rest, the book didn't live up to my expectations. Poor characterization simply killed the story for me. The characters were drawn in a strange way and their back stories were introduced awkwardly. I couldn't understand their motivations and actions. Too often they acted immaturely (Yvette Nichol) or weirdly hysterical (Clara Morrow, Yolande). Dialog was very stilted at times too, often I had no idea what people were talking about and why they found certain things funny.<br /><br />I suppose I should have cut <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/194243.Louise_Penny" title="Louise Penny" rel="nofollow noopener">Louise Penny</a> some slack, it was her first novel after all. But the book was rather poorly written even for the first effort. I am surprised <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/338691.Still_Life__Armand_Gamache___1_" title="Still Life (Armand Gamache, #1) by Louise Penny" rel="nofollow noopener">Still Life</a> managed to receive so much critical recognition and mainly positive Goodreads ratings. Did the mystery standards go down since Agatha Christie's death? I guess the success of this book is the biggest mystery to me...</span>
  <a data-text-id="4029160518530218752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1390823439?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=louise-penny">louise-penny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=mystery-thrillers">mystery-thrillers</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1390823439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12276946153338348819">Sometimes a memorable read needs to be revisited for a multitude of reasons.<br/><br/>Louise Penny lost her husband Michael this year. Her loss was so apparent in her latest offering, The Great Reckoning. As I turned the initial pages of this first book in the series, Still Life, I came upon the Acknowledgements that almost made me weep:<br/><br/>"This is for my husband Michael, who has created a life for us full of love and kindness. He allowed me to quit my job, pretend to write, then gave me unstinting praise ev</span>
  <span id="freeText12276946153338348819" style="display:none">Sometimes a memorable read needs to be revisited for a multitude of reasons.<br /><br />Louise Penny lost her husband Michael this year. Her loss was so apparent in her latest offering, The Great Reckoning. As I turned the initial pages of this first book in the series, Still Life, I came upon the Acknowledgements that almost made me weep:<br /><br />"This is for my husband Michael, who has created a life for us full of love and kindness. He allowed me to quit my job, pretend to write, then gave me unstinting praise even when what I produced was drivel. I've realised that anyone can be a critic but it takes a remarkable person to offer praise. Michael is that person." So you see, more than just words have gone on every page by Louise Penny. Far, far more.<br /><br />Chief Inspector Armand Gamache of the Surete du Quebec is introduced to us in Still Life as well as the tiny village of Three Pines. When an elderly former teacher has been found dead along a woodsy path, shock reverberates throughout the village. Was this a careless hunting accident or was there something more sinister going on? If so, who could ever have wanted the kindly Jane Neal dead?<br /><br />As you enter into an Armand Gamache book, you will pull back on the reins and slow the pace. Your eyes adjust to finite observations and attention to detail. Gamache's eyes sweep over every gesture, every careless article, and every door ajar. He tunes into every bit of dialogue with the words: "Tell me about it." And each storyline of every book in the series will sharpen your own sensitivities and your own sharpened skills.<br /><br />The truth is hard-hitting in Three Pines. One of their own is responsible in some way for Jane's death. Houses left unlocked at night soon become fortresses. Fear permeates like heavy smoke. Gamache brings along his trusted inspectors. They will soon discover that Three Pines will give up, unwillingly, multi-layered secrets. You will also meet the main characters who weave their way throughout the series.......the heart and the core of Louise Penny's offerings.<br /><br />Still Life begins the journey and is a must read to set the stage. The following books will grow in intensity, subject matter, character development, and heavy-duty crime. The Inspector Gamache Series is certainly not fluff as you will discover. It will expose you to the dastardly deeds at the hands of the respected and the not-so-respected of humanity. <br /><br />Ask any die-hard fan of Louise Penny and they will broadly smile at the mere mention of her name.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12276946153338348819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2512431150" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2512431150" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2512431150?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Matt by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/8530205-marty-fried">Marty Fried</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2512431150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1462585152372941606">Easily a 4.5 star read!<br/><br/>A strong recommendation from a friend helped me decide to embark on a binge of the Chief Inspector Armand Gamache series, penned by Canadian author Louise Penny. Her writing style and setting this novel in the bucolic community of Three Pines, Quebec, pulled me in early and kept me enthralled until the very end. Local artist and retired teacher, Jane Neal, was loved by many, which made the discovery of her body all the more troubling. With no known enemies, Jane’s death co</span>
  <span id="freeText1462585152372941606" style="display:none">Easily a 4.5 star read!<br /><br />A strong recommendation from a friend helped me decide to embark on a binge of the Chief Inspector Armand Gamache series, penned by Canadian author Louise Penny. Her writing style and setting this novel in the bucolic community of Three Pines, Quebec, pulled me in early and kept me enthralled until the very end. Local artist and retired teacher, Jane Neal, was loved by many, which made the discovery of her body all the more troubling. With no known enemies, Jane’s death could only have been an accident, though the small pool of blood and no visible weapon open many questions and require some police presence. Chief Inspector Armand Gamache, head of Homicide with the Sûreté du Québec, is called to Three Pines to investigate. Alongside his regular team is Agent Yvette Nichol, so new that she has never worked a scene. Gamache is sure to have his hands full trying to teach her while wrapping things up swiftly. With Thanksgiving turkeys cooking in ovens across town, no one wants to spend much time on what looks to be an accidental shooting with an arrow. While this might be the case, Gamache is worried that no arrow was found at the scene—it having been removed from Jane’s body—and no one has come forward to admit to the accident. As Gamache and the rest of the Homicide Squad begin piecing things together, they are confronted with a number of local citizens, all with their own flavourful take on events and tidbits about others in town. Gamache must parse through what he is being told and, at times, sift through the lies that some present to protect the more vulnerable in this community. Still, with Agent Nichol bumbling along and ostracizing herself from her superiors and others pushing for an open and shut case, Chief Inspector Gamache must be thorough and patient, for that is how one catches a killer! Penny pulls the reader in with this stunning debut story, which has me eager to see what else she has in this lengthy series. I will definitely be grabbing Book 2 in short order. Fans of police procedurals and Canadian mysteries will also find something worthwhile.<br /><br />I am so pleased to have found yet another Canadian author whose work falls within one of the genres I enjoy so much. Set in rural Quebec, the series opens with a lovely Canadian flavour, something that will enrich the reading experience and have it stand out in the genre. With this strong debut novel in the series, Penny provides the reader with some interesting backstory and some character development of Armand Gamache that will likely develop more thoroughly as I delve deeper into the series. Gamache is highly intelligent and down to earth as he investigates the crime before him, but seems to expect much from his team, no matter their time under his tutelage. He does not appear to suffer fools, but can extract information out of an unknowing suspect while enjoying his Tim Horton’s coffee. Penny’s descriptive nature has me highly interested in learning much more about the entire homicide team, all of whom will surely play important roles as the full series develops, but have laid the groundwork for being full of their own nuances. The story moves slowly, but there is no lack of momentum as Three Pines comes alive with each passing segment of the story. Penny keeps the reader in the middle of the investigation, dropping hints throughout as she pushes towards the reveal, which ties the entire experience together. With a new novel set to come out soon, I am happy to commence binge-reading to catch up in time to enjoy the latest release alongside series fans. I cannot wait!<br /><br />Kudos, Madam Penny, for intriguing me greatly. I am ready to take the challenge and see what Gamache does for me.<br /><br />Like/hate the review? An ever-growing collection of others appears at: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/">http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/</a><br /><br />A Book for All Seasons, a different sort of Book Challenge: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/248185-a-book-for-all-seasons">https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1462585152372941606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780312352554" href="/book/show/912984.Still_Life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80033559-kylie-d?shelf=atwi80b-2019">atwi80b-2019</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2930312482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer258578980193298936">An intriguing and intricately woven mystery, I was sucked in by this book from the start. Chief Inspector Gamache has been sent to a small town outside Montreal to investigate the murder of an elderly lady, to find she has been shot on a hunting trail during hunting season. Accident? Probably not, as she was shot by an arrow through the heart, something only a skilled archer could do. And with a thriving archery club in the town, there is no shortage of suspects.<br/><br/>As we get to know the quirky folk</span>
  <span id="freeText258578980193298936" style="display:none">An intriguing and intricately woven mystery, I was sucked in by this book from the start. Chief Inspector Gamache has been sent to a small town outside Montreal to investigate the murder of an elderly lady, to find she has been shot on a hunting trail during hunting season. Accident? Probably not, as she was shot by an arrow through the heart, something only a skilled archer could do. And with a thriving archery club in the town, there is no shortage of suspects.<br /><br />As we get to know the quirky folk from the township, we find many people are hiding things. But who would want to kill a harmless old lady? Does it have something to do with the painting she's entered in the local art competition? Gamache and his team have their work cut out for them as they sift through the information they gather to try to get to the truth.<br /><br />Louise Penny has written a little gem here. The characters are all so realistic, we could be sitting down to a cup of tea with them. The quaint setting of Three Pines comes to life and jumps off the page, and the story itself has me wanting to read more of this series. Recommended to all mystery lovers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="258578980193298936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1872645878" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1872645878" />
    <a title="Phrynne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne"><img alt="Phrynne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577753809p2/8655084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1872645878?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phrynne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phrynne" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne">Phrynne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1872645878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15415125638172816629">This was a pleasure to read. Imagine a detective who is happily married and is not an alcoholic! Discovering Chief Inspector Armand Gamache is a pleasure in itself!<br/><br/>I really enjoyed the setting, a small town in Quebec, and I became quite attached to several of the characters. They were quirky and a couple verged on going over the top but overall the author held it together.<br/><br/>An easy, comfortable read with just a bit of bite to it to keep it interesting. Consider me hooked on the series:)</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1277813807" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1277813807" />
    <a title="Candi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3639005-candi"><img alt="Candi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585187464p2/3639005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1277813807?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candi" href="/user/show/3639005-candi">Candi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30918623-still-life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=mystery-crime">mystery-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=dogdaysofsummer2017">dogdaysofsummer2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=canada-canadian">canada-canadian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1277813807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14585353624023772188"><i>"Three Pines wasn’t on any tourist map, being too far off any main or even secondary road. Like Narnia, it was generally found unexpectedly and with a degree of surprise that such an elderly village should have been hiding in this valley all along. Anyone fortunate enough to find it once usually found their way back."</i><br/><br/>I’ve seen this book and others in the Chief Inspector Armand Gamache series pop up so many times in my friends’ reviews and lists. And yet, I hesitated to read it for some time sinc</span>
  <span id="freeText14585353624023772188" style="display:none"><i>"Three Pines wasn’t on any tourist map, being too far off any main or even secondary road. Like Narnia, it was generally found unexpectedly and with a degree of surprise that such an elderly village should have been hiding in this valley all along. Anyone fortunate enough to find it once usually found their way back."</i><br /><br />I’ve seen this book and others in the Chief Inspector Armand Gamache series pop up so many times in my friends’ reviews and lists. And yet, I hesitated to read it for some time since I didn’t really consider myself a ‘series reader’ any longer. I felt that if I got hooked on a series, I would get ‘tied down’ and feel like I would have to set aside too many other wonderful books in order to continue with a series. Well, I’ve since become older and wiser, and series are no longer a thing of the past but another delightful option in a world where I can read whatever I want, whenever I choose! I’ve started several series over the past year or two, and have had my eye on this one for some time now thanks to the favorable feedback of many Goodreads’ friends. Having read this first in the series, I have to say I’m in for the long haul! I won’t rush through them, since as I mentioned, there are so many books yet to be read – but I plan to commit fully!<br /><br />The village of Three Pines is so charming – as in the quote above, I believe I am one of those folks who have found it and am hoping to be fortunate enough to find my way back. I’m not sure that Louise Penny intended that for me, but I’m reading into it that way regardless ;) I loved the descriptions of the little town, the surroundings, and the somewhat quirky characters. Sent to investigate the death of a gentle old soul named Jane Neal, Chief Inspector Armand Gamache from the Sûreté du Quebec is respectable, intelligent and a true gentleman. Such an appealing leading man all around. I am eager to learn more about him in the next several books. It seems no one would ever want to deliberately harm Jane – or would they? Inspector Gamache will do what he does best – listen and watch by inserting himself smack dab in the middle of the goings-on – in order to determine if her death was an accident or *gasp* a murder! <i>"Before his eyes the village of Three Pines seemed to slow right down. The insistence of life, the bustle and energy became muffled. The voices dropped, gaits slowed. Gamache sat back and did what he did best. He watched."</i><br /> <br />The cast of characters is quite entertaining, and I enjoyed getting to know each of them – even the not so pleasant ones I would likely sidestep in real life! Jean Guy Beauvoir, Gamache’s second in command, is another I am keen to watch develop further in later installments, and the pair make for a satisfying duo. I loved popping in at the bistro to see what everyone was eating and drinking, visiting the quaint little bookshop – who wouldn’t love that!, getting a glimpse inside some of the resident homes, and traipsing around in the local woods. Louise Penny also touches on some Quebecois culture which I hope she expands upon in later books, as this is an aspect that really appeals to me as well. Despite the idyllic aura of Three Pines, there are some complex relationships and dark secrets that draw the reader further into the intrigue. <br /><br />A well-written and delightful debut, Still Life is one I wouldn’t hesitate to recommend to anyone that loves a good little mystery set in captivating surroundings with very pleasing characterizations. 4 stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14585353624023772188" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1281167864" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1281167864" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24360539-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557534460p2/24360539.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1281167864?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/24360539-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250000644" href="/book/show/13539460-still-life">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Cozy mystery fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24360539-thomas?shelf=canada-crime">canada-crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1281167864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11615418204304550069">4.5 stars rounded down to 4 for a very well written cozy mystery. There is only 1 murder, and little violence.<br/>This is book 1 in the Armand Gamache mystery series. It takes place in Three Pines, Quebec, a mythical village close to the US border with Vermont. Gamache is the Chief of Homicide with the Surete du Quebec. He lives and is based in Montreal, but investigates murders province wide.<br/>He is called to Three Pines because of the suspicious death of Jane Neal, whose body was found in the woods </span>
  <span id="freeText11615418204304550069" style="display:none">4.5 stars rounded down to 4 for a very well written cozy mystery. There is only 1 murder, and little violence.<br />This is book 1 in the Armand Gamache mystery series. It takes place in Three Pines, Quebec, a mythical village close to the US border with Vermont. Gamache is the Chief of Homicide with the Surete du Quebec. He lives and is based in Montreal, but investigates murders province wide.<br />He is called to Three Pines because of the suspicious death of Jane Neal, whose body was found in the woods near Three Pines.<br />The author introduces a wonderful group of well drawn characters in this village. Gamache patiently investigates with the help of his team and does find who the killer is with the help of various villagers.<br />The investigation is shown to be a team effort, which is how most murders are solved in real life.<br />I was not sure who the killer was until the end. <br /> This part of Quebec has a fair number of anglophones, descendants of Loyalists who fled the US at the end of the US revolutionary war. Some of the tensions between anglophone vs. francophone are described with kindness. A family member gave me this book.<br />Two quotes:<br />A villager describing Gamache: "Ben had been expecting a francophone, perhaps even a unilingual French detective, so he'd spent a few minutes practicing his French, and how to describe his movements. Now this immaculate man with the trimmed mustache, the deep brown eyes looking at him over the rim of his half moon glasses, the three-piece suit(could that possibly be a Burberry coat?), the tweed cap with graying, groomed hair underneath, was extending his large hand-as though this was a slightly formal business occasion- and speaking English with a British accent. Yet he'd heard snippets of his conversation with his colleagues and that was definitely in fast and fluid French." <br />Three Pines: "It's a code. For the United Empire Loyalists. They settled all the land around here, except for the Abenaki of course.' In a sentence, Gamache noticed, Ben had dismissed a thousand years of native habitation. "But we're only a couple of kilometers from the border with the US states. When the people loyal to the crown during and after the War of Independence were fleeing, they had no way of knowing when they were safe. So a code was designed. Three pines in a cluster meant the loyalists would be welcome.'<br />Update July 7, 2019: My wife and I have just returned from visiting this part of Quebec. I did see 3 pine trees in a row, but no 3 pines in a cluster. We were looking for covered bridges though, not clusters of pine trees. We found 17 covered bridges.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11615418204304550069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_120763247" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120763247" />
    <a title="Richard Derus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus"><img alt="Richard Derus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494992210p2/3920693.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120763247?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard Derus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard Derus" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus">Richard Derus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120763247" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11743081859055749866"><b>Film Review</b><br/><br/>Book Rating: 4.5* of five<br/><br/><b>The Publisher Says</b>: Winner of the New Blood Dagger, Arthur Ellis, Barry, Anthony, and Dilys awards.<br/><br/>Chief Inspector Armand Gamache of the Sûreté du Québec and his team of investigators are called in to the scene of a suspicious death in a rural village south of Montréal and yet a world away. Jane Neal, a long-time resident of Three Pines, has been found dead in the woods. The locals are certain it’s a tragic hunting accident and nothing more but Gamache smells </span>
  <span id="freeText11743081859055749866" style="display:none"><b>Film Review</b><br><br>Book Rating: 4.5* of five<br><br><b>The Publisher Says</b>: Winner of the New Blood Dagger, Arthur Ellis, Barry, Anthony, and Dilys awards.<br><br>Chief Inspector Armand Gamache of the Sûreté du Québec and his team of investigators are called in to the scene of a suspicious death in a rural village south of Montréal and yet a world away. Jane Neal, a long-time resident of Three Pines, has been found dead in the woods. The locals are certain it’s a tragic hunting accident and nothing more but Gamache smells something foul this holiday season…and is soon certain that Jane died at the hands of someone much more sinister than a careless bowhunter.<br><br>With this award-winning first novel, Louise Penny introduces an engaging hero in Inspector Gamache, who commands his forces—and this series—with power, ingenuity, and charm.<br><br><b>My Review</b>: Oh, the raptures of a first novel that also inaugurates a mystery series! It's like your first piece of birthday cake as a kid...OMIGOD this is good wait whaddaya mean I gotta wait another whole year to get another one you stink and you're mean *waaahIwantmymommy*<br><br>But crafty old fifty-plussers like moi wait. We lurk behind the bakery, sniffing the ineffable esters of birthday cakes destined for the inexperienced and the impatient and the indiscriminate, mentally filing away those scents most closely followed by moans and slurps of ecstasy, biding our time and hoarding our book-calories (aka money) to see which annual yumyums consistently produce those sounds and smells.<br><br>Here it is, ladies and what-all-else, the first birthday cake from Canadian cake-baker Louise Penny, and my GOD was it worth the wait!<br><br>A friend sent this to me as a Christmas gift. It came after self-same friend raved and jumped up and down and yodeled the praises of the series, featuring Inspector Gamache of the Quebec Surete (I can't help myself, I hear Gestapo jackboots and Euro-sirens every time I see that word) and the odd, off-kilter inhabitants of Three Pines, Quebec. I was practically panting with eagerness to get this package, which when it arrived proved to contain *several* of the Gamache series.<br><br>Being a good Virgo, I snatched up the first in the series, and applied eyes to page. Steadily. For four hours. I was 2/3 through with the book then, and *forced* myself to put it down because a) I had to walk the dog, b) I had to feed my 91-yr-old aunt, and c) I had to pee.<br><br>Let's talk about mystery series for a minute. I like them, as readers of past reviews will yawningly recall, because they satisfy my need for order, for the world to work *right* for a change. I think a lot of people feel similarly to me. But a series, iteration upon iteration of similar plots/characters/motivations/dialogue...what makes a well-read consumer of Lit'rachure such as I, and so many fellow Goodreadsers, am/are seek these books out? Comfort? Yes, but... Ease? Yes, but... Quality.<br><br>Some of the best storytelling going on in literature today happens in mysteries and thrillers.<br><br>Yeup, you can love or loathe Grisham's writing, but you CANNOT fault, in any way, his eye for a story. You can fairly say it's not to your personal taste, but don't even TRY to say it's "not good." Likewise James Patterson, Stephen King, Iris Johansen, et alii. There is a reason these folks are bestsellers, and it is NOT that the People got no taste. It's that these are storytellers, entertainers, creators of worlds we-the-people want to inhabit if only for a moment.<br><br>As was Homer, may I remind the snobs. No one thought much about Homer's stuff, except that it was rollicking good fun. Nobody even bothered to write it down for a few centuries *after* writing was invented. Somewhere on the <i>Times</i> bestseller list is the work of the Homer our culture will be remembered for, and it's not likely to be Faulkner. (Horrible thought: What if it's HEMINGWAY?!?)<br><br>Louise Penny's Three Pines is a place I want to go and stay, eating Gabri's bounteous cooking and flirting with Olivier and lusting from afar at unattainable Peter and gossiping unkindly with Ruth...then settling in for a long, quiet snifter with Gamache and Beauvoir and Clara, to think it all through and come to a reasoned conclusion about life. I am there with these people, these words-on-page creations that have the life only a deep well of talent can water into existence. I believe them. I think you will, too.<br><br>I offer this moment from very near the end of the book, when Clara realizes who murdered her very best friend: <br><blockquote>Clara stared at her reflection in the window of {the victim}'s kitchen. A ghostly,frightened woman looked back. Her theory made sense. <br>Ignore it, the voice inside said. It's not your business. Let the police do their work. For God's sake, don't say anything. It was a seductive voice, one that promised peace and calm and the continuation of her beautiful life in Three Pines. To act on what she knew would destroy that life.<br>What if you're wrong? cooed the voice. You'll hurt a lot of people...But Clara knew the voice lied. Had always lied to her. Clara would know and that knowing would eventually destroy her life anyway.</blockquote><br>If that doesn't make you sprint out to get this book, nothing else I can say will.<br><br><b>+++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++</b><br>Rating: 2.5* of five<br><br><b>The Filmmaker Says</b>: When a beloved schoolteacher is found dead, the possibility of murder leaves the quaint town of Three Pines aghast in this crime drama based on the award-winning novel by Louise Penny. <a href="http://acorn.tv/franchise/stilllife" rel="nofollow noopener">The Film at Acorn.tv</a><br><br><b>The Film Review</b>: Well now. I don't know what cause Louise Penny to distance herself from the film made of her first novel, and so far as I am aware, she hasn't been public about the cause of her breach with the filmmakers.<br><br>The only actor I recognized in the cast was Gamache, played by Nathaniel Parker. I had a dizzy moment or two when I first saw Peter Morrow, playd by one <a href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm0389527/?ref_=tt_cl_t4" rel="nofollow noopener">Gabriel Hogan</a>. I was sure as sure could be that it was <a href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm0738433/?ref_=nv_sr_1" rel="nofollow noopener">Henry Rollins</a> with a bad dye-job and after a facelift. Then I wondered if permaybehaps Mr. Hogan was, errrmmm, a product of Rollins' rock-star years...no, born in 1973...so no go....<br><br>And do you now see the problem? I was able to trace these arabesques and follow these fancies because I was so very not wrapped up in the film. Parker does a rather blah job as Gamache, the lady who plays Clara is nothing special, we don't so much as hear BOO from Myrna, Gabri and Olivier appear to be acquaintances with a formal past. And then there are the police: Lacoste looks just right and isn't terribly busy onscreen, Jean-Guy is edgeless, but then there's Agent Nicol. She's perfectly cast for attitude, is <a href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm3208285/?ref_=tt_cl_t6" rel="nofollow noopener">Susanna Fournier</a>. Manages to be just like Nicol in the book.<br><br>Whatever the alchemy is that makes a film adaptation great is missing from this one. It's pretty to look at. The actors aren't bloody awful in the roles. The screenplay has the events in order. And at the end of the 88 minutes, I was utterly uninterested in seeing more.<br><br>Bad, bad sign.<br><br><a href="http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/deed.en_US" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="Creative Commons License" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380148217i/680962.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>This work is licensed under a <a href="http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/deed.en_US" rel="nofollow noopener">Creative Commons Attribution-NonCommercial-ShareAlike 3.0 Unported License</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11743081859055749866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_751363978" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/751363978" />
    <a title="Eduardo George" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25093909-eduardo-george"><img alt="Eduardo George" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/751363978?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eduardo George" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eduardo George" href="/user/show/25093909-eduardo-george">Eduardo George</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer751363978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15958604319940481304"><br/>Martha Stewart meets Agatha Christie on a very bad hair day. <br/><br/>I was recommended this author by a friend who is a great admirer of Ian Rankin and Stieg Larsson, so I was quite excited as I set out. Excitement soon turned to disappointment, followed by a sense of disbelief that writing so bad could be so well received by the reading public. And indeed win a prize, albeit one for novice crime writers.<br/><br/>The setting is an idyllic village near Montreal, populated with a cast of caricatures - aging bohemi</span>
  <span id="freeText15958604319940481304" style="display:none"><br />Martha Stewart meets Agatha Christie on a very bad hair day. <br /><br />I was recommended this author by a friend who is a great admirer of Ian Rankin and Stieg Larsson, so I was quite excited as I set out. Excitement soon turned to disappointment, followed by a sense of disbelief that writing so bad could be so well received by the reading public. And indeed win a prize, albeit one for novice crime writers.<br /><br />The setting is an idyllic village near Montreal, populated with a cast of caricatures - aging bohemian artists, a famous but misanthropic poet, a retired black psychologist, a gay couple who run, guess what, the bistro and bed and breakfast. I could continue. <br /><br />The hero inspector is an intelligent, intuitive and caring man who spends what little free time he has helping his wife stuff partridges with wild rice in the kitchen of his trendy Montreal apartment. His second-in-command is almost indistinguishable from him. <br /><br />By way of contrast we have some rough poor people, and a handful of one dimensional, over the top, emotionally challenged characters. <br /><br />All the nice people run around eating fragrant, freshly baked rolls stuffed with warm brie and black forest ham, while dabbling in solving the murder which has only ever so slightly ruffled the peace and tranquility of their lives. There is an abundance of golden leaves and drifting woodsmoke.<br /><br />The plot is disjointed, the pace is tediously slow, the characters are drawn with strokes so thick you can't make them out, the writing is seldom good and sometimes painfully bad. According to the cover, there was actually an editor. This is a book with very few redeeming features, other than the occasional telling description and flash of humour. <br /><br />Whodunnit? I really didn't care enough to find out. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15958604319940481304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_495527809" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/495527809" />
    <a title="Florence (Lefty) MacIntosh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh"><img alt="Florence (Lefty) MacIntosh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346034704p2/10856439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/495527809?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Florence (Lefty) MacIntosh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Florence (Lefty) MacIntosh" href="/user/show/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh">Florence (Lefty) MacIntosh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780751547382" href="/book/show/10466342-still-life">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Detective mystery &amp; Canadian Lit fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=lit-canada">lit-canada</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=detective">detective</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=debut">debut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=rural-smalltown">rural-smalltown</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=awards">awards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=mystery-crime">mystery-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer495527809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16693432751921453501">NO SPOILERS. Her debut, entertaining, well written and deserving of its literary awards. A traditional detective novel, the murder unraveled by careful observation - felt like a breath of fresh air after my normal diet of forensics mysteries. A murder disrupts the peace in Quebec’s heartland where <i>"The only reason doors were locked was to prevent neighbors from dropping off baskets of zucchini at harvest time"</i>. A rural setting, quiet pace and lack of gore has some pegging this as a cozy mystery,</span>
  <span id="freeText16693432751921453501" style="display:none">NO SPOILERS. Her debut, entertaining, well written and deserving of its literary awards. A traditional detective novel, the murder unraveled by careful observation - felt like a breath of fresh air after my normal diet of forensics mysteries. A murder disrupts the peace in Quebec’s heartland where <i>"The only reason doors were locked was to prevent neighbors from dropping off baskets of zucchini at harvest time"</i>. A rural setting, quiet pace and lack of gore has some pegging this as a cozy mystery, disagree. On the surface seems just a pleasant story placed in a picturesque artsy community but there's depth. Undercurrents of homophobia, the tension between Anglo &amp; Francophone’s. <br />Atmospheric without being gloomy, nice change from the Canadian novels I’ve read lately. Fascinating characters, Chief Inspector Armand Gamache a standout. What? A detective who’s respectful and loves his wife, brilliant without a drop of arrogance – appealingly flawed, if anything overly compassionate? Refreshing...<br /><i>"He always felt a pang when looking at the hands of the newly dead, imagining all the objects and people those hands had held. The food, the faces, the doorknobs. " </i><br />Tension provided courtesy of a smug young rookie agent, Yvette Nichol. As her mentor Gamache tries to stem her arrogance by teaching her humility, the power of <i>
  <b>"I’m sorry, I don’t know, I need help, I was wrong." </b>
</i> Plan on reading the next in the series just to see if she smartens up. <br />Loved the role the painting ‘Fair Day’ plays in the mystery. Didn’t figure out the murderer but that’s no surprise, I rarely do. <b>For it’s genre a solid 4.5 stars.</b> And in case you’re wondering if places like this actually exist - the answer is yes:)<br /><br /><b>Cons: </b> Way too many characters and while the majority are well fleshed out a few are ridiculously exaggerated. No one is as superficial as Yolande Fontaine, as smug as Agent Yvette Nichol – couldn’t take either of them seriously.<br /><br /><i>“A fire had been laid and lit, outside the storm moaned and called the leaves from the trees.”</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16693432751921453501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2347210322" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2347210322" />
    <a title="Peter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63168028-peter"><img alt="Peter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516912354p2/63168028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2347210322?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter" href="/user/show/63168028-peter">Peter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63168028-peter?shelf=group-reads">group-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63168028-peter?shelf=around-the-world">around-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63168028-peter?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63168028-peter?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63168028-peter?shelf=global-read">global-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2347210322" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8689951298865130733"><b>Dissolution</b><br/><i>Still Life</i> is the first book in the Chief Inspector Armand Gamache, of the Sûreté du Quebec, series. It is a great murder mystery that has a depth of possible suspects and expands to encapsulate human psychology and community dynamics. The number of characters and plot twists were really well balanced so the reader isn't overwhelmed with complexity yet it's extensive enough to keep our imagination wondering who the murderer is and what the motive might be.<br/><br/>The opening lines of the nove</span>
  <span id="freeText8689951298865130733" style="display:none"><b>Dissolution</b><br /><i>Still Life</i> is the first book in the Chief Inspector Armand Gamache, of the Sûreté du Quebec, series. It is a great murder mystery that has a depth of possible suspects and expands to encapsulate human psychology and community dynamics. The number of characters and plot twists were really well balanced so the reader isn't overwhelmed with complexity yet it's extensive enough to keep our imagination wondering who the murderer is and what the motive might be.<br /><br />The opening lines of the novel states. <i>“Miss Jane Neal met her maker in the early morning mist of Thanksgiving Sunday. It was pretty much a surprise all around.”</i> The surprise is, who could unexpectedly murder a well-loved elderly artist and ex-teacher, and why? Jane was killed with an arrow and we are treated to an informative overview of bows and arrows – which I found very interesting.<br /><br />Throughout the story, I was drawn towards different suspects for quite legitimate reasons and I would say that if you guess the murderer early on, it will be as much luck as investigative deductions. To give equal credence to several possible murderers is a real craft in writing a whodunit and Louise Penny achieves that really well. It’s all about creating motive, opportunity and the capability to carry out the horrific act of murder. In the story, Oscar Wilde is quoted as saying that <i>“Conscience and cowardice are the same things. What stops us from doing horrible things isn’t our conscience but the fear of getting caught.”</i><br /><br />Gamache has an engaging style that is really appealing, he listens, he observes, he has an analytical mind. He helps develop his team and has a fundamental desire to support new recruits and imparts wisdom in assessing a person’s character and principles, such as our ability to make choices. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I watch. I’m very good at observing. Noticing things. And listening. Actively listening to what people are saying, their choice of words, their tone. What they aren’t saying. … It’s as simple and as complex as that. And as powerful. So when I’m observing, that’s what I’m watching for. The choices people make.”</i>
</blockquote><br />He is also pragmatic and firm and will make tough choices when necessary. As a consequence, his team are extremely loyal and cohesive. Well, the established team members are!<br /><br />This book is a highly crafted murder mystery that I highly recommend and managed to read it as part of my GR monthly group read. Thanks for nominating this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8689951298865130733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2080843665" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2080843665" />
    <a title="PattyMacDotComma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1128612-pattymacdotcomma"><img alt="PattyMacDotComma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577835191p2/1128612.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2080843665?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PattyMacDotComma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PattyMacDotComma" href="/user/show/1128612-pattymacdotcomma">PattyMacDotComma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30918623-still-life">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">mystery lovers, especially cosy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=aa">aa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=mystery-crime-thriller">mystery-crime-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2080843665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6950729522835973644"><b>4+★</b><br/><b>“He always felt a pang when looking at the hands of the newly dead, imagining all the objects and people those hands had held. The food, the faces, the doorknobs. All the gestures they’d made to signal delight or sorrow. And the final gesture, surely, to ward off the blow that would kill. The most poignant were the hands of young people who would never absently brush a lock of gray hair from their own eyes.”</b><br/><br/>Chief Inspector Gamache of the Sûreté du Quebec has been called to the woods near the </span>
  <span id="freeText6950729522835973644" style="display:none"><b>4+★</b><br /><b>“He always felt a pang when looking at the hands of the newly dead, imagining all the objects and people those hands had held. The food, the faces, the doorknobs. All the gestures they’d made to signal delight or sorrow. And the final gesture, surely, to ward off the blow that would kill. The most poignant were the hands of young people who would never absently brush a lock of gray hair from their own eyes.”</b><br /><br />Chief Inspector Gamache of the Sûreté du Quebec has been called to the woods near the small village of Three Pines, where the body of a popular retired schoolteacher has been found. Even at this stage of his career, he’s still surprised by violent death.<br /><br /><b>“Gamache always hoped maybe someone had gotten it wrong, and there was no dead body. But there was no mistaking the increasingly rigid Miss Neal.”</b><br /><br />Nope. No mistake. I am late to Louise Penny and her inspector’s fan club, but I intend to stay the distance. I thoroughly enjoyed meeting the residents of the village – not ignorant hillbillies and not hippie dropouts, but an interesting mix of old-timers and artists.<br /><br />Gamache is bilingual, and the English-speaking residents are surprised to hear him speak English with a House of Lords accent. He’s adaptable, gentlemanly and ingratiating, although he comes down pretty hard on a young agent assigned to assist with the case but who can’t help blurting out her own opinions when asked to keep them to herself. He’s also devoted to his wife with whom he shares everything to get her opinion.<br /><br />I grew very fond of him, as well as the many other characters. I thought I’d lose track, but Penny does such a good job of describing them and their personalities and quirks, that they became distinct individuals.<br /><br />Clara is an artist who often seems to have crumbs stuck to her clothes and is generally a bit eccentric and untidy. In this instance, she was <b>“coming toward them, a duck barrette clinging to a few strands of hair, getting ready for the final flight.</b><br /><br />This takes place during the winter, cold, sometimes wet and miserable, but the food is wonderful in the local bistro and B&amp;B. The gay couple who run it welcome everyone to the fireside as they come in from their investigations, the perfect cosy mystery setting.<br /><br />Myrna is an enormous black woman who runs the local bookshop and enjoys her food as much as she enjoys her books. She seems generally accepted, but <b>“being black, she knew that singular expression when people saw her as furniture.”</b><br /><br />I’m not black, but I’m female, and I’ve been in plenty of situations where that’s exactly what it feels like as the men direct their conversations only to each other. ARGH#*!<br /><br />There are also a few teenaged boys who may be implicated, and a father worries <b>“because he knew every parent of a teenage boy fears they’re housing a stranger.”</b><br /><br />As it turns out, everybody is pretty much under suspicion at one time or another, and I changed my mind more than once about where I thought the clues were leading.<br /><br />At least the fact I’ve waited so long to be introduced to the Chief Inspector means I have another dozen books to read. Plus, this debut has the lowest rating, so they must keep getting better!!<br /><br />An interview with the author about her troubled past is here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2W_tUxI4Mww#action=share">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2W_tU...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6950729522835973644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
